From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Jul  1 18:32:37 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Brian {Hamilton Kelly})
Date: Mon, 01 Jul 2002 18:32:37 +0100
Subject: [Xitami] Strange "notification" received; from a list member?
Message-ID: <49441@dsl.co.uk>

I've just received the following strange e-mail, claiming that a message
of mine was deleted (by the recipient) without reading.  So I checked
back on the message of mine referenced therein, and found that it was
something I posted to this list exactly two months ago, on the 1st May.

Has anyone else been receiving similar strange "notifications"?  Can the
list owner confirm, or otherwise, that the purported sender of this mail
is a subscriber to the list?

Incidentally I don't, as a matter of routine, include a Return-Receipt-To
header in my mails, and am pretty sure that the list exploder doesn't
(because otherwise everyone would be being inundated with these sorts of
notifications all the time.

[All headers retained, for obvious reasons]

Hmm, exactly two months: could it be that Russell is so far behind on
collecting traffic from his ISP that the latter has deleted it?  (I know
that my ISP does something similar; if mail is neither delivered by SMTP
[for those of us that run our own smtpd] nor collected by POP3, then it
will be bounced back to the originator [as required by RFC-[2]821] after
30 days.  But surely this notification is insufficient to comply with
that sort of bounce mandated by the RFC?)

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Jul  2 10:12:22 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Tue, 02 Jul 2002 11:12:22 +0200
Subject: [Xitami] Strange "notification" received; from a list member?
In-Reply-To: Message from bhk@dsl.co.uk (Brian {Hamilton Kelly})
 of "Mon, 01 Jul 2002 18:32:37 BST." <49441@dsl.co.uk>
Message-ID: <20020702091222.8BC04ADF5A@basilica.la.naos.co.nz>

In message <49441@dsl.co.uk>, Brian {Hamilton Kelly} writes:
>I've just received the following strange e-mail, claiming that a message
>of mine was deleted (by the recipient) without reading.  

You're not alone.  I've received several of them as well.

>Can the list owner confirm, or otherwise, that the purported sender of this 
>mail is a subscriber to the list?

He is not a subscriber under the address in question.  There is a
subscriber under an address which I suspect forwards to that address.

If these "deleted unread" messages continue to arrive then I'll probably
remove that "likely candidate" and advise them they've been removed
until they can confirm their mail system isn't the cause of the
messages.

>[for those of us that run our own smtpd] nor collected by POP3, then it
>will be bounced back to the originator [as required by RFC-[2]821] after
>30 days.  But surely this notification is insufficient to comply with
>that sort of bounce mandated by the RFC?)

Any such bounce message should probably be omitted for Precedence: bulk
and other similar "mailing list" messages anyway.  (I've not checked
the RFCs recently but I suspect they say something similar.)  At very
least they should be sent to the mailing list software, not anywhere
else.

Anyway I am aware of the issue, and the message someone else posted that
it was being investigated.  There will be a small grace period to fix
the issue, and if not I'll do what I can at the mailing list end to
minimise the problem.   (However the "deleted unread" messages appear to
relate to old messages already "received", and bypass the mailing list,
so there is a limit to what I can do.)

Ewen McNeill
Mailing List Administrator

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Jul  2 15:35:26 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Joop van der Star)
Date: Tue, 2 Jul 2002 16:35:26 +0200
Subject: [Xitami] REQUEST_URI
Message-ID: <NFBBLIBEFPPGHEFOLMJCEEKACEAA.j.vanderstar@library.uu.nl>

To Xitami list,

I use Xitami on a Win98 system in order to run a PHP application called SDMS
(simple Document Management System).
After a lot of learning (PHP, MySQL and Xitami) the applications runs. There
is only one part that doesn't work an that is the download function, where
you can download a document that is listed in SDMS, There is a server
variable called $REQUEST_URI that has no value.
I guess that one need some kind of confuguration setting within Xitami.

Does anyone know a solution to this problem.

I use SDMS version 1.1.4, PHP version 4.2.1 an dXitami version 2.5b

m.vr.gr. Joop van der Star, j.vanderstar@library.uu.nl
tel. (+31)(0)30 253 6624, fax. 253 9292

Universiteitsbibliotheek Utrecht, Postbus 16007, 3500 DA  Utrecht

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Jul  2 16:23:15 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ervin Kosch)
Date: Tue, 02 Jul 2002 11:23:15 -0400
Subject: [Xitami] REQUEST_URI
References: <NFBBLIBEFPPGHEFOLMJCEEKACEAA.j.vanderstar@library.uu.nl>
Message-ID: <3D21C563.30306@lmgnet.com>

$REQUEST_URI is not a standard HTTP 1.1 enviromental varible. Its only 
used in Apache 1.21 and above(see http://www.apache.org).

Try $SCRIPT_NAME or $PATH_TRANSLATED in it's place. You might have more 
luck with these.

Also, below are some links to to similar problems with the varible:

http://www.object-craft.com.au/projects/albatross/albatross/tug-content1.html
http://www.phpbuilder.com/forum/archives/5/2001/12/3/23977
http://forums.mercuryboard.com/index.php?a=topic&t=773

trying to use an ssi command with xitami <!--#include file="filename.txt" -->
and the thing just wont work.

My computer will recognize the .shtml extension as a webpage and read that 
page correctly, but whatever file I included does not show up.

Example - marylamb.shtml looks like this:
<html>
<head><title>Mary's lamb</title></head>
<body>
Mary had a little lamb, it's <!--#include file="fleece.txt" --> as snow.
</body>
</html>

Fleece.txt looks like this:
fleece was white

But whenever I open marylamb.shtml it just says
Mary had a little lamb, its as snow.

Both files are in my 'webpages' directory.
Is there some option in xitami that I need to turn on in order to make ssi 
work?

--part1_c.2a704a40.2a5365ed_boundary

	charset="iso-8859-1"
Content-Transfer-Encoding: quoted-printable

I have emulated exactly what you did and all is working fine.
Some things to consider:

Insure that SSI is enabled by opening the Administration screen, =
clicking on Configuration, clicking on SSI, then making sure the SSI =
enabled is checked on.

I also noticed that (and it might be a typo) that below you have =
Fleece.txt as the filename but when you call it in the SSI it is =
fleece.txt so your case switching may be a problem.

-Rob

This is weird but probably a normal issue considering the circumstances....

Some people can access my server and some can't.. here's my settings:

I'm using DNS2GO to manage my dynamic IP, so it assigns a regular web
address: http://surfto.27south.com.
All is well with that. In my Xitami settings it states my Hostname is
http://default and the IP addresses are 192.168.1.100 and 127.0.0.1. That
seems normal to me.

My log files are filled with people traveling through the site as normal,
but then I talk with people specifically who cannot access the site even
though the server is running and I am able to access it at the same time
they are not.

Is there a clue in here somewhere for me?

Thanks in advance,

-Rob

References: <c.2a704a40.2a5365ed@aol.com> <002201c22210$8635f760$6401a8c0@rdemarti> <000901c22270$b61c8880$6401a8c0@rdemarti>

I know some ISP's, especially cable and DSL based ISP's, use a content 
caching system.  So it could be 24 hours before they will show your content.
It maybe a matter of waiting.

Some also mentioned changing your IP address.  I'm assuming you either 
on a LinkSys router or similar setup which will not allow you to do that 
without disabling your mini-intranet.

From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Brian {Hamilton Kelly})

In message <3.0.6.32.20020624091136.00a26550@mail.shininglightpro.com>
   "Thomas J. Hruska" writes:

> However, the problem still won't go away since anyone sniffing for packets
> can grab any HTTP Authorization header and store it away for a later replay
> attack (MD5 hashes included).  What is worse is that Xitami doesn't have
> DIGEST mode available which means that the username:password combination is
> only Base64 encoded (and makes it _VERY_ easy to obtain access to "secure"
> areas - e.g. remote /admin access).  Even with DIGEST mode, it still
> doesn't stop a replay attack since the HTTP protocol doesn't have any
> secure handshaking methods.
> 
> So, hashing the files might help some locally, but won't stop anyone from
> attacking the server remotely.  The problem is not necessarily with Xitami
> but also has to do with the inherent weakness of the HTTP protocol.

There's an easy answer to that: don't remotely administer the server via
HTTP!  Either walk into the machine room (or use SSH sessions) and use a
text editor.

HTTP-based administration only exists for the lazy and those who cannot
imagine use of a computer without having thinks to click.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Thu Jul  4 20:41:32 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Thomas J. Hruska)
Date: Thu, 04 Jul 2002 15:41:32 -0400
Subject: [Xitami] Plaintext passwords on Bugtraq (again)
In-Reply-To: <49470@dsl.co.uk>
Message-ID: <3.0.6.32.20020704154132.00a5ef68@mail.shininglightpro.com>

At 08:14 AM 7/4/2002 +0100, Brian {Hamilton Kelly} writeth:
>In message <3.0.6.32.20020624091136.00a26550@mail.shininglightpro.com>
>   "Thomas J. Hruska" writes:
>
>> However, the problem still won't go away since anyone sniffing for packets
>> can grab any HTTP Authorization header and store it away for a later replay
>> attack (MD5 hashes included).  What is worse is that Xitami doesn't have
>> DIGEST mode available which means that the username:password combination is
>> only Base64 encoded (and makes it _VERY_ easy to obtain access to "secure"
>> areas - e.g. remote /admin access).  Even with DIGEST mode, it still
>> doesn't stop a replay attack since the HTTP protocol doesn't have any
>> secure handshaking methods.
>> 
>> So, hashing the files might help some locally, but won't stop anyone from
>> attacking the server remotely.  The problem is not necessarily with Xitami
>> but also has to do with the inherent weakness of the HTTP protocol.
>
>There's an easy answer to that: don't remotely administer the server via
>HTTP!  Either walk into the machine room (or use SSH sessions) and use a
>text editor.

Another answer would be to set up some sort of handshaking in the HTTP
protocol (however, I don't see the IETF moving to change that very
quickly).  It isn't that difficult to add a level of security that would
make it much more difficult to crack.  ESMTP already does this with the
header in the first message from the server.  You then run an MD5 hash with
your password and the string sent in the first message and send it with the
EHLO command.  Much more secure than even DIGEST since a replay attack
requires cracking the username and password before a replay can occur.

However, I agree with the use of SSH tunnelling for remote admin.  Yet,
HTTP could offer a little more security than it does right now (which is
basically squat).


          Thomas J. Hruska -- shinelight@shininglightpro.com
Shining Light Productions -- "Meeting the needs of fellow programmers"
                  http://www.shininglightpro.com/

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Jul  5 17:57:30 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (bernd hohmann)
Date: Fri, 05 Jul 2002 17:57:30 +0100 (MEZ)
Subject: [Xitami] Sokrates 1.6
Message-ID: <200207051557.g65FvD4W029326@sxpublic.nxrda.imatix.net>

Sokrates 1.6 is available (http://runner.conacom.de)

We worked hard since the last release and can provide support for the
latest Java Servlet API 2.3 (see read.me) now.

Changes since last public release 1.3


05.07.02 1.6  
Added documentation
ServletContext#getRequestDispatcher(..).
ServletContext#getNamedDispatcher(..).
Information about operating system logged.
Attribute javax.servlet.context.tempdir points now to a java.io.File
with a tempdir.
Runner#check_semaphore() is a thread now.
update to API 2.3, not implemented are methods with Java 1.2 return
values (Map, Set).
update to API 2.2.
Session-ID is configurable in the sessionmanager config now
(session_id)
SessionCookie expires with -1 (browser session) again.
removed "queued_startup" parameter. ServletInstance uses LockObject for
synchronizing .init() and .run() which allows faster startup.
Fixed race condition in ServletInstance

16.06.02 1.5  
Speedups in MonitoredExecution (caching, thread reusing). 10 times
faster now.
Event system for shutdown/dispose.
Fixed problem with various un-closed streams (Properties).

14.06.02 1.4  
RunnerClassLoader: added local path to container classpath if classpath
is empty.
getServetName() & getRemoteHost() returning RDNS name (see:
reverse_dns=1/0 in container config).
added logscn_options.
ServletInstance#processError(..): uses rootcause of error now.

Depending on what you are using for a net connection, your internet provider gives a 
Dynamic or Static IP.  It is not a setting you really chose unless your internet provider 
has definatly provisioned you a static ip.  If you "do" have a static IP you'll need your IP, 
your netmask, their router #, and their DNS #s.  I forget the name of the config utility for 
setting this up on the ethernet under linux (been a bit and I haven't used linux that 
much).  But I'm sure someone could tell you.  Just make shure you have your required 
information from your provider.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Jul  5 17:50:00 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Control-Freak)
Date: Fri, 5 Jul 2002 12:50:00 -0400
Subject: [Xitami] Dynamic IP to Static IP
References: <002e01c2243b$845c3120$0a02a8c0@test>
Message-ID: <02ee01c22444$012f5350$2c182341@crestron>

You can't do it yourself, unless you order a static IP from RoadRunner.
But, that might be expensive (don't know, never checked the price).  So,
instead,  you can go with an IP forwarding service like www.dns2go.com .
You point your URL (with your domain provider (or just use
www.yourdomain.dns2go.com for free)) to dns2go (They will tell you the DNS
IPs).  Then, you run  their client software on your server that updates
dns2go with your current IP.  Then dns2go re-directs all domain requests to
your current IP.

There is one more problem, however.  RoadRunner blocks port 80 (standard
html port).  So you have to tell Xitami to run your webserver at a port like
6800 or something (read how in the Xitami docs).  You also have to tell the
dns2go client software to portforward requests with a www. prefix to
whatever port you use.  And, bring your FTP port back down to 20 (see Xitami
docs).

Then, your html URL will be www.yourdomain.com and your FTP URL will be
ftp://yourdomain.com .  You have to use the www. prefix or dns2go will not
know to portforward html requests to your new html port (6800 or whatever
you picked), and you have to make sure not to use it with FTP requests, or
dns2go will portforward those to the same port as your webserver.

Its all free (and pretty transparent) unless you want email.  Then they
charge a bit.

Good Luck,

- Jay

> But, that might be expensive (don't know, never checked the price).  So,
> instead,  you can go with an IP forwarding service like www.dns2go.com .
> You point your URL (with your domain provider (or just use
> www.yourdomain.dns2go.com for free)) to dns2go (They will tell you the DNS
> IPs).  Then, you run  their client software on your server that updates
> dns2go with your current IP.  Then dns2go re-directs all domain requests
to
> your current IP.
>
> There is one more problem, however.  RoadRunner blocks port 80 (standard
> html port).  So you have to tell Xitami to run your webserver at a port
like
> 6800 or something (read how in the Xitami docs).  You also have to tell
the
> dns2go client software to portforward requests with a www. prefix to
> whatever port you use.  And, bring your FTP port back down to 20 (see
Xitami
> docs).
>
> Then, your html URL will be www.yourdomain.com and your FTP URL will be
> ftp://yourdomain.com .  You have to use the www. prefix or dns2go will not
> know to portforward html requests to your new html port (6800 or whatever
> you picked), and you have to make sure not to use it with FTP requests, or
> dns2go will portforward those to the same port as your webserver.
>
> Its all free (and pretty transparent) unless you want email.  Then they
> charge a bit.
>
> Good Luck,
>
> - Jay
>
> ----- Original Message -----
> From: ShweMyint
> To: xitami-post

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Jul  5 18:41:19 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (ian)
Date: Fri, 05 Jul 2002 13:41:19 -0400
Subject: [Xitami] Dynamic IP to Static IP
In-Reply-To: <021901c22448$0d353030$2f28a8c0@rcolmstead.com>
Message-ID: <200207051741.g65Hfg4W030437@sxpublic.nxrda.imatix.net>

In the last few days I have seen several people talk about dynamic name 
services from the likes of dns2go and tzo.com. I am sure they work just 
great but I have never used their services having been a long time user 
of another service that I haven't seen mentioned recently. I stress, I 
am just a user of dyndns and not affiliated with them in any other way!

I use the services of dyndns.org - and having looked at both dns2go and 
tzo.com I would suggest that if you are interested and have a need for 
dynamic IP services you look at what's available from dyndns.org, 
especially from a cost standpoint on the advanced offerings! Everyone, 
including dyndns.org have the free services for basic dynamic IP 
management and will give you a xxxxx.dyndns.org username but the built 
in clients in the LinkSys router and Netgear routers will automatically 
keep your dyndns.org address pointing in the right direction, so to me 
that's a plus (although maybe this is true for the others too... but 
from what I saw on the other sites the client is something you have to 
run on the server itself and if it is a private IP behind a NAT device 
like a Netgear or similar, you may be out of luck!)

The advanced features of dyndns are inexpensive though - just a ONE off 
donation of $30 for each www.yourdomainname.com you want to use and 
you're off and running, managing your own DNS (and they make it easy if 
you are a beginner) that you can always have resolve directly to your 
dynamic IP for anything you want to use it for, including mail (MX) 
support... in fact I have found no real limitations to their services 
at this price... they even support an offline redirect, web hopping 
(for services where port 80 is blocked) and various other tricks.

Anyway, that's all I will say... I am sure dns2go and tzo are great, 
I'm not saying they aren't... but just from what I saw on prices and 
since no one else had mentioned it... I thought I would tell you about 
dyndns.org!

www.dyndns.org

Subject: [Xitami] Xitami, Linux and PHP = my brain is fried...
In-Reply-To: <00b201c2241f$97c2b020$0239a8c0@thomas>
Message-ID: <3.0.6.32.20020705185601.00a2ae68@mail.shininglightpro.com>

At 02:29 PM 7/5/2002 +0200, Thomas Løcke writeth:
>Recently I've installed Xitami on a Slackware 8.1 Linux. I'm having severe
problems getting PHP to work.
>
>Both CGI and SSI works flawlessly, but PHP simply just wont. I'm open for
suggestions, tips and good ideas - anything that might make this combo
work. :o)

What does your [filters] section look like?  You need to add an entry that
points at the PHP executable for the .php, .phtml, etc. file extensions

If you are having problems with PHP not redirecting properly, you will want
to use the XiFusion wrapper program which fixes that problem.

Hope this helps!

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sun Jul  7 21:36:48 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Thomas J. Hruska)
Date: Sun, 07 Jul 2002 16:36:48 -0400
Subject: [Xitami] Xitami crashing after FTP
In-Reply-To: <3D2856E4.21521.48B807@localhost>
Message-ID: <3.0.6.32.20020707163648.00a41d88@mail.shininglightpro.com>

At 02:57 PM 7/7/2002 -0400, WhiteShepherd writeth:
>   I am running Xitami for OS/2.  I went with a dedicated FTP client as
the FTP in Xitami 
>was corrupting files during heavy use.  I have now run into the problem
that Xitami 
>crashes a LOT after users upload files to their web pages with the FTP.
Is there a way 
>or a setting that can stop this or perhaps reduce this?  Any help/replies
would be greatly 
>apreciated!  Thanks!

Xitami has a known crashing problem with heavy server usage when the FTP
server is enabled.  Xitami also has a serious DoS/DDoS issue with large
numbers of CGIs running under Windows (and slows to a crawl with heavy CGI
usage under Linux).

The solution is to get a dedicated FTP server.  The FTP server in Xitami is
not meant for heavy-duty use and tends to crash the server.  Xitami without
FTP is very stable, but you need to be picky in the CGI arena (e.g. PHP)
till that gets fixed.

Hope this helps!


          Thomas J. Hruska -- shinelight@shininglightpro.com
Shining Light Productions -- "Meeting the needs of fellow programmers"
                  http://www.shininglightpro.com/

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sun Jul  7 22:01:59 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Otto)
Date: Sun, 07 Jul 2002 23:01:59 +0200
Subject: [Xitami] Installing PHP
Message-ID: <200207072301590447.0048A9FB@smtp.xs4all.nl>

I have installed PHP. when i test it on localhost it's working fine.
When i test it remote i get the following error message:

***********
Security Alert! The PHP CGI cannot be accessed directly. 
This PHP CGI binary was compiled with force-cgi-redirect enabled. This means that a page will only be served up if the REDIRECT_STATUS CGI variable is set, e.g. via an Apache Action directive.

For more information as to why this behaviour exists, see the manual page for CGI security.

For more information about changing this behaviour or re-enabling this webserver, consult the installation file that came with this distribution, or visit the manual page.
***********

In my php.ini file i have this:

; cgi.force_redirect is necessary to provide security running PHP as a CGI under
; most web servers.  Left undefined, PHP turns this on by default.  You can
; turn it off here AT YOUR OWN RISK
; **You CAN safely turn this off for IIS, in fact, you MUST.**
; cgi.force_redirect = 1

; if cgi.force_redirect is turned on, and you are not running under Apache or Netscape
; (iPlanet) web servers, you MAY need to set an environment variable name that PHP
; will look for to know it is OK to continue execution.  Setting this variable MAY
; cause security issues, KNOW WHAT YOU ARE DOING FIRST.
; cgi.redirect_status_env = ;

any ideas?




From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sun Jul  7 22:24:34 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (=?iso-8859-1?Q?Thomas_L=F8cke?=)
Date: Sun, 7 Jul 2002 23:24:34 +0200
Subject: [Xitami] Installing PHP
References: <200207072301590447.0048A9FB@smtp.xs4all.nl>
Message-ID: <00c001c225fc$b11365e0$0601a8c0@vendetta>

If you're running Xitami under Windows you have to disable the
cgi.force_redirect. Locate it in the php.ini file and change it to 0. At
least that was how I made it work.. :o)

Thomas

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Jul  8 16:09:40 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul Reid)
Date: Mon, 8 Jul 2002 11:09:40 -0400
Subject: [Xitami] Which Version For XP?
In-Reply-To: <jUsT.aNoTheR.mEsSaGe.iD.102606751419366@email.beginners.co.uk>
References: <jUsT.aNoTheR.mEsSaGe.iD.102606751419366@email.beginners.co.uk>
Message-ID: <160519635666.20020708110940@rci.rutgers.edu>

> Xitami to run on my Windows XP Home Edition ... somewhat confused as to which
of the many versions that are listed on
http://www.imatix.com/html/xitami/index2.htm#download I should download.

Don't go there. That page has been out of date for years. Go to:

http://www.xitami.com/download.htm

Do you want the stable old 2.4 series or the 2.5 series with new
features not fully debugged? If in doubt, go with 2.4, and
specifically 2.4d9

Win 95/NT bw3224d9.exe [705 Kb] works fine but has to be started
manually (or with trickery). For occasional testing, this is what I
use.

Win NT service bs3224d9.exe [740 Kb] can be told to auto-start, even
before you log-in. This is what I use for unattended full-time
servers.

The "Vanilla Win95" version will probably work, but the NT versions
will be more stable (XP is just NT with new decorations). The Alpha,
Unix, OS2 etc versions won't work on MS Windows. You don't sound
like you want the Source Kit, you want the Install Package.

2.5 adds some new frills, including (I think) a different
implementation of SSI. 2.4's SSI needs Perl installed, so it may be
better to use 2.5 if stability is not paramount. (FWIW, several
people here are running 2.5 perfectly well in heavy use.)

 -PRR

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Jul  9 00:30:19 2002

I would check out a port sniffer. 
Turn the OTHER FTP server completely off ... at the service panel.
Then see what is listening on the ports.
I would think that there are two apps fighting for the same port.

Unless two programs are fighting for the same memory or communication channel, 
they should co-exist.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Jul  9 14:05:19 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Thomas J. Hruska)
Date: Tue, 09 Jul 2002 09:05:19 -0400
Subject: [Xitami] Xitami crashing after FTP
In-Reply-To: <3D2A2A5C.27162.76AA8B3@localhost>
References: <200207082340.g68Neh4W007889@sxpublic.nxrda.imatix.net>

At 12:12 AM 7/9/2002 -0400, WhiteShepherd writeth:
>Ok ran a netstat -s to check.  FTPD is only using 21 and Xitami is
listening to 80 and 81.  
>Here is a common error befor a crash: 
>
>No such file or directory

Xitami could not find the file or directory to load.  Sounds like the FTP
server is doing some sort of caching it shouldn't...or Windows could be
corrupted or Xitami is corrupted or something is not right.

>Broken pipe

Possibly a further result of the file not opening.  My guess here is that
Xitami is attempting to use a file or socket anyway.  At this point there
is trouble later on whatever the case is.

>Socket operation on non-socket

The client socket has been closed or we are accessing memory we don't own...

>Clean-memory assertion failed - xitami.c (208)

This is (strangely) located at the end of Xitami's execution in main().
I'm surprised the program got that far.  However, it is due to Xitami
attempting to use or access memory it doesn't own or no longer owns.
Xitami appears to be on its way out the door to avoid that great core dump
in the skies whatever the case is.

>Abnormal program termination

It looks like the program exited but then the CPU took over and realized a
memory fault took place during the clean-memory scan.

>core dumped

Hence, the core dump.  So much for avoiding it...

>Any of this make sense?

Nope.  Just extrapolating on what seems to be taking place.

>On 8 Jul 2002 at 16:30, Gunnar Swan wrote:
>> I would check out a port sniffer. 
>> Turn the OTHER FTP server completely off ... at the service panel.
>> Then see what is listening on the ports.
>> I would think that there are two apps fighting for the same port.

There should be no problem here.  Any Windows sockets provider worth its
salt will only allow one program to own a single port on one IP at one
time.  So, if there are two server programs contending for the same port,
only one gets it.

>> Unless two programs are fighting for the same memory or communication
channel, 
>> they should co-exist.

This could be, but with Windows you never know what the OS will decide to
do next :)  (I'm not an advocate of any OS...I just haven't found any that
I really like).

Hope this helps!


          Thomas J. Hruska -- shinelight@shininglightpro.com
Shining Light Productions -- "Meeting the needs of fellow programmers"
                  http://www.shininglightpro.com/

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Jul 10 00:53:44 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Wed, 10 Jul 2002 11:53:44 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] Xitami crashing after FTP
In-Reply-To: Message from "Thomas J. Hruska" <shinelight@shininglightpro.com>
 of "Tue, 09 Jul 2002 09:05:19 -0400." <3.0.6.32.20020709090519.00a5c4c8@mail.shininglightpro.com>
Message-ID: <20020709235344.AAFC3ADFA2@basilica.la.naos.co.nz>

In message <3.0.6.32.20020709090519.00a5c4c8@mail.shininglightpro.com>, "Thomas 
J. Hruska" writes:
>>Clean-memory assertion failed - xitami.c (208)
>
>This is (strangely) located at the end of Xitami's execution in main().
>I'm surprised the program got that far.  However, it is due to Xitami
>attempting to use or access memory it doesn't own or no longer owns.

FWIW, no, what it means is that the memory usage tracking in the
library that Xitami uses (SFL) has detected that not all the memory
allocated has been freed up.  Typically this means that not all the
"free my memory" logic has been run, which often happens in a crash
situation.  This is primarily present in the code for the benefit of
developers, because if not all memory gets given back each time it is
taken, then eventually the program will take all the memory in the
system!  (It's enabled in the "user" versions as well to try to catch
those hard-to-find situations that occur only for real users.)

>>Abnormal program termination
>
>It looks like the program exited but then the CPU took over and realized a
>memory fault took place during the clean-memory scan.
>
>>core dumped
>
>Hence, the core dump.  So much for avoiding it...

These two are actually _caused_ by the clean memory assertion failing;
the state of the program in that situation is saved to help in tracking
down where things might have gone astray.  This is mostly only of use to
developers though, who can match it up with their source code.

Ewen


-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Jul 10 04:44:13 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Stefan Pantazi)
Date: Tue, 9 Jul 2002 20:44:13 -0700
Subject: [Xitami] Neophyte seeks Info 101
In-Reply-To: <3D2BB514.52042065@tscnet.com>
Message-ID: <DAECIFPNFLGIHMJEOGHMEELOCCAA.spantazi@uvic.ca>

Hi,

> myself. At this point I'd like to accomplish one
> concrete, significant goal. I would like to install an elementary
> web document just for testing purposes, and log onto it from the
> public library. Just to make it happen; to prove that it can be
> done. That's all. Nothin' fancy.

When you installed Xitami, you were prompted for some install folder
(usually c:\xitami or c:\program files\xitami). Inside the install folder
there is, among other things, a subfolder called webpages. Anything you
place there can be accessed from the entire world, which include your public
library. For example if you create a page called test.html and place it
there, you can access it remotely using http://YourServerIP/test.htm
I suggest that you rename your test page as index.html which enables you to
access it only by http://YourServerIP
you'll probably find out later why.

I guess this proves that you can further create your own webhost.

Good luck.

Stefan

Content-Type: text/plain; charset=us-ascii; format=flowed
Content-Transfer-Encoding: 7bit

If I'm not mistaken what your asking is 'Where do I put the files'.  There is a folder at 'C:\XITAMI\WEBPAGES'.  You can get rid of everything inside the folder and put your stuff there.  Thats it for files.

As to logging in from a library and seeing yourself, you'll have to know your public side IP#.  To you it may look like 127.0.0.1, to the outside world you look like '213.52.0.1'.  I put up a little tool that you use to find your public side IP# at http://yumyum.ws/ipplayground.php  Just go there on your server machine and write down your number.  Remeber each time you log off and back on the internet this public side IP# will change.  You can't trust what a program called 'WINIPCFG.EXE' says is your IP#/  Your ISP maybe doing some funky stuff to keep you from running a server.

Other little tidbits about webservers in general:
	127.0.0.1 and the words localhost are the same thing to a computer.
	If want to play around with your setting type in 'http://127.0.0.1/admin'
	Xitami does not do most server side scripting when you install it.  Your have to install things like PHP and Cold Fushion
	Windows based webservers don't care about case(uppercase and lowercase) on file names.  Example: http://127.0.0.1/MYFile.htm is the same as http://127.0.0.1/myfile.htm to a Windows based webserver.  Unix and Linux servers are not so forgiving.  Remember that if your going to put these files onto another server watch your case.
/

should be, yes?

web document just for testing purposes, and log onto it from the

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Jul 10 15:36:53 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul Reid)
Date: Wed, 10 Jul 2002 10:36:53 -0400
Subject: [Xitami] Neophyte seeks Info 101
In-Reply-To: <3D2BB514.52042065@tscnet.com>
References: <200207100116.g6A1GS3Z088767@smtpzilla1.xs4all.nl>
 <3D2BB514.52042065@tscnet.com>
Message-ID: <78166538299.20020710103653@rci.rutgers.edu>

> I would like to install an elementary web document just for
> testing purposes, and log onto it from the public library.

Open the stock top-page that comes with Xitami (default.htm or
index.htm) with wordpad or your HTML editor, scribble "Hello from
selinvict!" on the top, and verify that you see the change with
http://127.0.0.1 (and http://localhost should also work.

Now... to see the page from anywhere else in the world, you need to
know your IP number. If you are on hard-wire, DSL, Cable etc, that
info may be hidden in Network Neighborhood or any special toy that
comes with your net-connect. If you use phone-modem, you get a
different IP number every time you connect. (This may be true of
some high-speed links too, but they stay connected for long
periods.) And some versions of Windows seem very reluctant to tell
you the IP number presently assigned to a phone-modem connection.
What may be easiest is to find a Web-Forum that not only logs IP
numbers but tells you what your IP is.

Anyway, find out what your IP number is. Say the dial-up gave you
321.123.12.13. Leave the dial-up connected and run over to the
Library quick (before the dial-up drops the line or times-out).
Enter http://321.123.12.13 at the library websurfer and you should
see "your page".

Or maybe not. Dial-ups go down a lot. MANY home ISPs block
webservers. They may be using a proxy, where the IP you see at home
is not the IP that is seen by the outside world (and the proxy
server translates packet IP numbers on the fly).

In today's internet, putting up a webserver on a home connection is
not always easy. You rarely get a Fixed IP number with a Home
account. Home webservers tend to be bandwidth hogs, so the ISPs
costs are high. Also ISPs _sell_ Commercial Accounts, so anything a
home user doesn't really need (like fixed IP) is deliberately foiled
to urge you to convert to a (more expensive) Commercial account.

 -PRR

I once ran postnuke (a phpnuke descendant) with xitami 3.4d9 and php 4.0.5 
without any problems. Don't understand why I should need XiFusion or 
something. BTW, I think there is too much advertising for this and some 
other products on this list (apart from Xitami of course).
There were indeed some problems, but they were all implementation-related 
and could most often be found in the  various discussion boards and 
buglist. Especially the redirection problem, which is a known bug (has been 
half a year ago, I wonder that it still is) which, as far as I recall, 
stems from an incorrect use of the php redirect function, namely usage of 
relative paths in the redirect which is not conformant with the HTTP 
specification.
_Maybe_ Apache with compiled-in php _corrects_ this improper use. I don't know.
But apart from that (looking at the code of nuke) I can't see any relation 
to the actual webserver used.
BTW, in my opinion, there is no reason to think that any php product 
whatsoever depends on the webserver in use.

Tony

It sure is. I am running a web server with 8-10 domain names at www.trushosting.com. 
First you either need to signup for DNS services. I would suggest www.myserver.org. All 
the help you need is on their site. Second register a domain name, I use 
www.DomainWizardry.com. When you sign up for a myserver.org account your will be given 
name servers, e.g. ns.myserver.org etc. When you signup for your domain name you will 
need to add those name servers. That is pretty much it. There are alot of other ways to 
doing this including running your own DNS instead of myserver.org, but it is much more 
complicated.

Hope this helps,

Jon

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Thu Jul 11 18:50:59 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Marcio Marchini)
Date: Thu, 11 Jul 2002 13:50:59 -0400
Subject: [Xitami] IP numbers,etc.
In-Reply-To: <3D2DCC7F.C7C7E89F@tscnet.com>
Message-ID: <001b01c22903$8421bf00$0100a8c0@celeron2k>

| But I am wondering, is it possible to give a page
| a more durable address - say, a URL or a domain
| name? I'm sure the answer is yes, but can anyone
| give me a pointer on how to make this happen?


	You can register a domain ($20 / year) and then use www.zoneedit.com to host
the DNS service for you (free).

	Then you configure the computer which has a dynamic IP to tell zoneedit when
its IP changes. I do that from a Linux box. I run a script every 10 minutes
(because I do not have a hook for when my IP changes at the Linksys router, so I
just do it blindly / periodically). All it does is to visit a URL. Just by
visiting that URL at ZoneEdit they update the IP address for my domain. So, the
name will be constant but the IP may change as often as you want. All this is
documented at ZoneEdit, you've got to read the instructions there.

	So, I just give friends the name for my computer (say www.mycomputer.com) and
they can connect to it, even though I have a dynamic IP with an ADSL provider.


marcio


From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Thu Jul 11 19:07:26 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ervin Kosch)
Date: Thu, 11 Jul 2002 14:07:26 -0400
Subject: [Xitami] IP numbers,etc.
References: <3.0.5.32.20020710192540.00da5de0@vvm.com> <3D2DCC7F.C7C7E89F@tscnet.com>
Message-ID: <3D2DC95E.8090300@lmgnet.com>

You've graduated from webhost 101 to 201 now.

You have several options:
    1. Buy a static IP from your ISP.  If your ISP supports static(not 
changing) IP's that you'll pay anywhere from $ .01 to $20 extra a month.
    2. Get a DNS forwarding service.  These service work by linking a 
third level domain(Example: myname.tzo.com) to your IP address.  You 
then put a little program on your server. That program will every few 
minutes yells out to the service and say "I'm here" so to keep you IP# 
fresh. If watch this mail list people will give you serveral services. 
 I personally like TZO.com but other like DNS2GO.com and ww.myserver.org 
work just as well..  Depending on the level of service the offer the 
services will run you from free to $100/month.
    3. Make your own service.  I have a couple of domains that point to 
my home system.  So if someone types in home.yumyum.ws they hit my main 
server which then redirectes them to my server in my house.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Thu Jul 11 19:30:04 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul Reid)
Date: Thu, 11 Jul 2002 14:30:04 -0400
Subject: [Xitami] IP numbers,etc.
In-Reply-To: <3D2DCC7F.C7C7E89F@tscnet.com>
References: <3.0.5.32.20020710192540.00da5de0@vvm.com>
 <3D2DCC7F.C7C7E89F@tscnet.com>
Message-ID: <133266929233.20020711143004@rci.rutgers.edu>

>  is it possible to give a page a more durable address - say, a URL
> or a domain name?

"Easy way": get a Fixed IP address. That's how we used to do all
internet machines. Each school was given a block of IP numbers. At
each school a"hostmaster" person or office would assign IP numbers
to new machines, and that IP number is entered in the machine's TCP
configuration file.

Since people prefer typing names instead of numbers, a system
evolved so if you type a name where an IP number would be, the
computer contacts a name-server to translate the name to an IP
number. "DNS" is a Dynamic Name Server (it can be updated
constantly, compared to older systems that were harder to update).
Generally each school maintains a DNS server and contracts another
school to be a back-up in case of trouble.

Al Gore commercialized the InterNet, but ISPs follow the same
pattern. They have a block of IP addresses they can give to
customers, and maintain DNS servers to translate names to numbers.

So you get an IP number, you reserve names for your domain and each
machine, you enter those names and IP numbers in a DNS server. Then
anybody who types the name of your machine will get the IP number
and connect to your machine. Easy.

The DNS server has to be easy to find and very reliable. It is
possible to run your own DNS server but you usually want to have
someone else with an established DNS system to handle it.

A problem with that is: the world is running out of IP numbers. And
anyway it is silly to permanently assign an IP number to a dial-up
user who only needs it a few hours a month. A dial-up service with
10,000 customers often has only 1,000 modems and so only needs 1,000
IP addresses. You get an IP address when you connect, and you lose
it when you disconnect, and next time you will probably get a
different IP number.

Another side is: cable-modem/DSL is "always on" but the ISP may need
to change IP numbers as they grow their system. Customers won't know
how to change their IP numbers. So they ask you to use DCHP, a
protocol that assigns IP numbers when you connect and can re-assign
if needed. (PoET is another variant of DCHP-like service, adapted
for spread networking.) Or to be honest: many ISPs deliberately
change IP numbers from time to time, just to make it hard for you to
run a busy server on a "home" account, so you will pay more for a
Business account.

There is a way to get around impermanent IP numbers. Others have
pointed you to the Dynamic DNS services. When you start your
machine, or your IP number changes, your machine tells them what
your IP number is today. Their DNS server is registered (with the
master DNS systems) to be the DNS server for your domain. When
people type your machine name, they end up at that DNS server which
gives them the latest IP number for you. It is not perfect:
sometimes intermediate DNS servers hold old info longer than they
should. But as you see, it works good for jon and Marcio.

http://www.zoneedit.com/doc/dynamic.html?

Yes, Dynamic Dynamic Name Server sounds redundant. But in fact there
is an extra level of "dynamic" in these systems. Traditional DNS is
managed by a hostmaster, who can make changes any time she feels
like it. DDNS allows users to update info very frequently without
human attention.

For many reasons, it is often better to off-load the whole chore to
a commercial Web Host: someone with a fast connection, established
DNS, and racks of servers they rent-out. Do-it-yerself can be fun,
and sometimes the best way, but a goos web host service can be more
reliable and possibly cheaper all considered.

 -PRR

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Jul 12 03:11:47 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Thomas J. Hruska)
Date: Thu, 11 Jul 2002 22:11:47 -0400
Subject: [Xitami] OT: PHP-Nuke?
In-Reply-To: <5.1.0.14.2.20020712011137.00aad380@pop.chello.at>
References: <001001c228e8$300d0ac0$2c838282@vance2>
 <3.0.5.32.20020710192540.00da5de0@vvm.com>
 <5.1.0.14.2.20020711115443.00aabb18@pop.chello.at>
Message-ID: <3.0.6.32.20020711221147.00a2ce78@mail.shininglightpro.com>

At 01:23 AM 7/12/2002 +0200, TW writeth:
>Vance,
>didn't mean to be mean with my comment.
>Over time it just got a feeling that a newbie might come to the conclusion 
>that xifusion is a more or less manadatory prerequisite for sucesfully 
>running any php-projekt together with xitami. And this is definitely not 
>the case. In some cases it may be a quick and welcome  workaround to some 
>problem, in general i think its rather a matter of misconception to wrap a 
>coldfusion server around a php-engine.
>Most of all, I believe that virtually no problem with a php-projekt has 
>something to do with the webserver in use.

Tony, the only thing XiFusion does for PHP is correct redirection and a few
minor issues dealing with the environment.  When you use the header()
function in PHP under Apache, Apache will automatically modify the redirect
if it is not an absolute HTTP-compliant URL and may perform additional
processing locally (depends on the situation).  XiFusion essentially does
the same thing, but is actually a side-effect of ColdFusion support.  All
XiFusion does is prepare, start an application, and process the results
passing them back to the server for further processing.  The code base is
something to the tune of 700 lines of C code, so it does quite a bit to fix
Xitami.

I will agree that it won't solve all of the world's problems and isn't
always the perfect solution, but it does work well where redirection issues
arise.  PHP will work fine until you encounter a script that uses relative
redirects.  At that point you either have to change the script, modify
Xitami's source, or use a wrapper like XiFusion.

To test this out try the following:

------index.php------
<?
  header("Location: index2.php");
?>
---------------------

------index2.php------
<?
  echo "Hi There!\n";
?>
---------------------

During the first test don't use XiFusion.  The browser will "hang" because
it does not understand the relative 'Location' header (and isn't required
to according to the HTTP/1.1 standard):

HTTP/1.1 301 Redirect
Server: Xitami v2.4d9
Location: index2.php
...

XiFusion v2.6 corrects this problem by making the relative URL an absolute
URL:

HTTP/1.1 301 Redirect
Server: Xitami v2.4d9
Location: http://localhost/index2.php
...

HTTP/1.1 200 Ok
Server: Xitami v2.4d9
Content-Type: text/html
Content-Length: 10

Hi There!


As you can see, XiFusion does have use in the area of PHP redirects.
Personally, I don't use redirects since they take too long compared to just
include()'ing the file.

Hope this helps!


          Thomas J. Hruska -- shinelight@shininglightpro.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Jul 12 03:32:48 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Thomas J. Hruska)
Date: Thu, 11 Jul 2002 22:32:48 -0400
Subject: [Xitami] Multiple IP Addresses
In-Reply-To: <200207112057.g6BKuv4X018217@sxpublic.nxrda.imatix.net>
Message-ID: <3.0.6.32.20020711223248.00a2ce78@mail.shininglightpro.com>

At 06:25 PM 7/11/2002 -0330, jon writeth:
>Hi:
>
>I am running a Windows Web Server and I have multiple IP addresses from my
ISP. They are 
>programmed into a Cisco 800 series router provided by my ISP. My problem
is this, I need 
>multiple IP addresses assigned to the web server for virtual hosts. Some
of my clients 
>require SSL certs. I am leaving the transfer of these clients to my server
because I do 
>not no how to get these IPs assigned to my server.

SSL is extremely CPU intensive as calculating/generating keys and
behind-the-scenes session management is a very complex process.  You will
want to have enough processing power behind the server to handle all
SSL/TLS and normal HTTP requests.  Too many SSL/TLS requests can quickly
drag a server to its knees and HTTP will be less responsive as a result.

You mentioned Windows Me.  I tried at one time to assign multiple IPs to
one network card by manually editing the registry and it worked somewhat.
I don't know how much mileage you will get from it.  A quick search on
Google found this link:

<http://www.wown.com/j_helmig/multiipa.htm>

Hope this helps!


          Thomas J. Hruska -- shinelight@shininglightpro.com
Shining Light Productions -- "Meeting the needs of fellow programmers"
                  http://www.shininglightpro.com/

This is exactly my point. If I want to set a http-header (in any script 
langugage) I don't want the webserver or anything else to correct this for 
me. I want an error to be thrown if something is wrong. People working in 
this environment try to write portable code, but webservers unsolicited 
correcting things destroy portability and readability.

My opinion:

-) modify xitamis source: NO WAY
-) use a wrapper: POOR SOLUTION, camouflages lost portability (and raises

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sat Jul 13 00:19:52 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Jay Moore)
Date: Fri, 12 Jul 2002 19:19:52 -0400
Subject: [Xitami] IP numbers,etc.
References: <3.0.5.32.20020710192540.00da5de0@vvm.com> <3D2DCC7F.C7C7E89F@tscnet.com> <133266929233.20020711143004@rci.rutgers.edu>
Message-ID: <002b01c229fa$a5fa6ad0$bab24104@JAYP4KAPEYL7EU>

> how to change their IP numbers. So they ask you to use DCHP, a
> protocol that assigns IP numbers when you connect and can re-assign
> if needed. (PoET is another variant of DCHP-like service, adapted
> for spread networking.) Or to be honest: many ISPs deliberately
> change IP numbers from time to time, just to make it hard for you to
> run a busy server on a "home" account, so you will pay more for a
> Business account.
>

were'd you learn this from?

DHCP is designed to assign the same IP to the same adapter if the network
permits it. each NIC has a specific identifier code, somehow (and I have no
clue how) each NIC sniffs out the DHCP server, and talks to it. then, based
on the info the DHCP server is given, a IP is assigned. a good example is
me. I have an external DSL modem/router and use DHCP. using a standard
network switch DHCP assignes each NIC a public IP. they've only changed when
the network did. for example, up till last week, the NIC in my computer was
4.63.10.123, same as it was the day I got DSL and was using it to test the
connection (it was in a second PC, I was using a USB NIC) and when I
switched back, it recieved the exact same IP address, amazing

PoET isn't a protocol, it's a program for PPPoE which I'm not sure how it
works.

Dynamic DNS was already explained.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sat Jul 13 20:56:35 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Neco Computers)
Date: Sat, 13 Jul 2002 14:56:35 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] (no subject)
References: <200207131902.g6DJ2n4X009288@sxpublic.nxrda.imatix.net>
Message-ID: <OE64XqtFpsTfQqfJD9w0000b271@hotmail.com>

> What is that best way to send E-mail through CGI Perl scripts, using
Xitami? Also if you
> can supply some Perl Syntax for doing so. I am use to UNIX, and I'm not
sure how to do
> this on a Windows server.

You can use sockets to send email:

  use Net::SMTP;
   my $smtp = Net::SMTP->new($smtp_server, Debug => 0) || die "unable to
create Net::SMTP object $smtp_server.";
   $smtp->mail($Webmaster);
   $smtp->to($Email);
   $smtp->data();
   $smtp->datasend("From: $Webmaster\n");
   $smtp->datasend("Subject: $subject\n");
   $smtp->datasend("\n");
   $smtp->datasend($message);
   $smtp->dataend();
   $smtp->quit();

You can either hard code the your email address or have it passed in from
the variables like is set up here.

Neil Finlayson
http://neco.pages.d2g.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Jul 15 10:31:51 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (=?iso-8859-2?Q?Janko_Slavi=E8?=)
Date: Mon, 15 Jul 2002 11:31:51 +0200
Subject: [Xitami] Does Xitami support content-encoding?
In-Reply-To: <3.0.6.32.20020711221737.00a2ce78@mail.shininglightpro.com>
Message-ID: <001101c22be2$75b7d3a0$1e5002c1@ladiskjanko>

I have used the added perl code as a hitami *.html filter (for
compression). Does anybody know why  my IE6 doesn't decodes the data? 

Thanks in advance.

janko

*******************perl***************************
#!/usr/local/bin/perl

use strict ;
local ($^W) = 1; #use warnings ;

use Compress::Zlib ;

binmode STDIN;
binmode STDOUT;
my $x = deflateInit()
   or die "Cannot create a deflation stream\n" ;

my ($output, $status) ;
while (<>)
{
    ($output, $status) = $x->deflate($_) ;

    $status == Z_OK
        or die "deflation failed\n" ;

    print $output ;
}

($output, $status) = $x->flush() ;

$status == Z_OK
    or die "deflation failed\n" ;

print $output ; 

*******************perl***************************

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Jul 15 15:08:31 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (ian)
Date: Mon, 15 Jul 2002 10:08:31 -0400
Subject: [Xitami] IP numbers,etc.
In-Reply-To: <002b01c229fa$a5fa6ad0$bab24104@JAYP4KAPEYL7EU>
Message-ID: <200207151409.g6FE9r4W000585@sxpublic.nxrda.imatix.net>

> DHCP is designed to assign the same IP to the same adapter if the
> network permits it. each NIC has a specific identifier code, somehow  
>(and I have no clue how) each NIC sniffs out the DHCP server, and     
> talks to it.

For what it's worth and this isn't the networking 101 mailing list... 
but the DHCP server is listening on the broadcast address of whatever 
subnet everything is set to (usually in a 24bit subnet that would be 
x.x.x.255)... If there are routers between the subnet of where the 
client is and the (different) subnet of where the DHCP server actually 
lives on then the router(s) will have a helper address programmed in of 
where to forward on the DHCP request from the client... This is a 
really simple answer and I won't go into any more detail - if 
anyone wants to understand subnets, subnet masks and bootp broadcasts 
etc. in more detail then you will find plenty of information on the web.

-Ian



From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Jul 15 15:41:32 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Thomas J. Hruska)
Date: Mon, 15 Jul 2002 10:41:32 -0400
Subject: [Xitami] Does Xitami support content-encoding?
In-Reply-To: <001101c22be2$75b7d3a0$1e5002c1@ladiskjanko>
References: <3.0.6.32.20020711221737.00a2ce78@mail.shininglightpro.com>
Message-ID: <3.0.6.32.20020715104132.00a89cf8@mail.shininglightpro.com>

At 11:31 AM 7/15/2002 +0200, =?iso-8859-2?Q?Janko_Slavi=E8?= writeth:
>I have used the added perl code as a hitami *.html filter (for
>compression). Does anybody know why  my IE6 doesn't decodes the data? 

IE doesn't support that header as far as I know.  Actually, to be brutally
honest, both IE and Netscape rely on the HINTERNET set of functions
provided by Windows.  That set of functions wastes bandwidth by (usually)
sending out two requests for a webpage instead of one (for GET, two GET
requests - for POST, one POST and one GET).  I wouldn't be surprised if IE
depends on HINTERNET to do the entire decoding/translation and doesn't do
it.  Netscape might do post processing on the data if that header exists.

Hope this helps!


          Thomas J. Hruska -- shinelight@shininglightpro.com
Shining Light Productions -- "Meeting the needs of fellow programmers"
                  http://www.shininglightpro.com/

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Jul 15 15:37:35 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul Reid)
Date: Mon, 15 Jul 2002 10:37:35 -0400
Subject: [Xitami] Elementary PHP/mySQL
In-Reply-To: <3D31C851.7243A6ED@tscnet.com>
References: <001401c22ae4$aa907860$1e01010a@fast> <3D31C851.7243A6ED@tscnet.com>

> It seems that PHP/mySQL is quite the thing to learn these days.

And if it were simple enough to explain it all here, then everybody
would be an expert and it wouldn't be "quite the thing".

And of course this mail-list is primarily for the webserver, not the
add-ins.

But here's the nutshell. Get PHP from the obvious place. Install it.
Read the documentation. As I recall, it is pretty clear about how to
hook it into a webserver. (Hint: in Xitami Admin, Filters, ".PHP" =
"C:/PHP/PHP.EXE" or something like that.)

I think PHP comes with sample pages.

Get PHP doing things first. In many ways, PHP is almost all you need
for many things. It has some database functionality built in.

But when you are sure you need an SQL-level database, get that,
install it, read the documentation.

Much info for PHP and mySQL is available on-line at the obvious
websites.

 -PRR

In-Reply-To: <002b01c229fa$a5fa6ad0$bab24104@JAYP4KAPEYL7EU>
References: <3.0.5.32.20020710192540.00da5de0@vvm.com>
 <3D2DCC7F.C7C7E89F@tscnet.com> <133266929233.20020711143004@rci.rutgers.edu>
 <002b01c229fa$a5fa6ad0$bab24104@JAYP4KAPEYL7EU>
Message-ID: <94600053601.20020715110208@rci.rutgers.edu>

> each NIC has a specific identifier code, somehow (and I have no
> clue how)

Every ethernet NIC has a unique serial number (MAC number) burned
into ROM. I have not disassmebled any cable-modem boxes but they
must have the same or similar functionality (possibly in the cable
head-end rather than the modem, considering the origins of 2-way
cable TV).

> DHCP is designed to assign the same IP to the same adapter if the
> network permits it.

DCHP uses whatever rules the admin sets.

Traditionally, you get ("lease") an IP for a period of time, an hour
or a week or "indefinite", and can renew the lease when it expires.
And traditionally it provisionally reserves the MAC=IP association
for hours or weeks after the DCHP lease expires unrenewed. If you
come back on-line within that time, and the DCHP server has not been
forced to give "your" IP to another NIC, then you get the same one
again.

However, give some people a tool and they abuse it. Some home ISP
services aggressively thrash DCHP so you won't keep the same IP
number for very long. After all, they sell fixed IP service at a
higher price, so why let you have the same thing for cheap?

 -PRR

------------- Original message text ------------------
Received: Wednesday, February 20, 2002, at 7:27 AM
From:     Francis Turner <francis.turner@freesbee.fr>
To:       Xitami list <xitami@lists.xitami.org>
CC:       
Subject:  [Xitami] Xitami bug with relative redirects
 
Using the standard CGI.pm you can (theoretically) redirect people to a 
URl doing something like
print $query->redirect("destination.url"). This prints two lines to STDOUT

Status: 302 Moved
location: destination.url

And normally you get a redirect from there.

It works is my destination.url is a fully defined 
http://host/path/file.html or similar

But I have found 2 bugs in this with Xitami when one uses a non absolute URL

with a file only relative url (just file.html) it chops of the leading 
character to produce a redirect to ile.html in the ROOT of the webserver 
. i.e. the absolute URL is http://host/ile.html
with a path and file relative url (/path/file.html) the redirect never 
completes and xitami just sits there serving up nothing until you hit 
cancel - conceivably there is a timeout after 120 seconds or whatever 
but I didn't wait that long.

This does not appear to occur with Apache which handles both relative 
URLs just fine. Arguably this is a bug with the redirect generator as  
RFC 2616 (http 1.1) section 14.30 states that only absolute URIs are 
allowed for the location field, but it would be nice to see it 
documented if not fixed.

14.30 Location

   The Location response-header field is used to redirect the recipient
   to a location other than the Request-URI for completion of the
   request or identification of a new resource. For 201 (Created)
   responses, the Location is that of the new resource which was created
   by the request. For 3xx responses, the location SHOULD indicate the
   server's preferred URI for automatic redirection to the resource. The
   field value consists of a single absolute URI.


Francis

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Jul 15 18:52:41 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Brian {Hamilton Kelly})
Date: Mon, 15 Jul 2002 18:52:41 +0100
Subject: [Xitami] (no subject)
Message-ID: <49562@dsl.co.uk>

In message <OE64XqtFpsTfQqfJD9w0000b271@hotmail.com>
   "Neco Computers" writes:
> > What is that best way to send E-mail through CGI Perl scripts, using
> Xitami? Also if you
> > can supply some Perl Syntax for doing so. I am use to UNIX, and I'm not
> sure how to do
> > this on a Windows server.
> 
> You can use sockets to send email:
> 
>   use Net::SMTP;
>    my $smtp = Net::SMTP->new($smtp_server, Debug => 0) || die "unable to
> create Net::SMTP object $smtp_server.";
>    $smtp->mail($Webmaster);

Hmm; interesting.  Presumably the mail() function issues an SMTP "MAIL
FROM: <$Webmaster>" and awaits a positive response?  What happens if it
gets a temporary (or permanent) error response?

>    $smtp->to($Email);

and then a "RCPT TO: <$Email>".  Again, there are various legitimate
responses to this, and only a few of them indicate success.

>    $smtp->data();

followed by a "DATA" command.  What happens to the script if any of these
operations encounter a non-success response from the remote SMTP server?

>    $smtp->datasend("From: $Webmaster\n");
>    $smtp->datasend("Subject: $subject\n");
>    $smtp->datasend("\n");

OK, that's two header lines, and the blank line that separates the header
from the body.  Does Net::SMTP automatically insert such (nowadays
mandatory under RFC-2822) headers as "Date:"?

>    $smtp->datasend($message);

Presumably the datasend() function is capable of sending the embedded
newslines?

>    $smtp->dataend();

which presumably sends the "." on a line of its own, to terminate the
DATA transfer.

What happens if the remote end fails to accept the message at this point?
RFC-2821 makes it quite clear that unless the SMTP client has received a
"success" code following the end of that part of the exchange, it must
NOT assume that the mail has been successfully sent, and undertake to
requeue it in some fashion.

>    $smtp->quit();

It strikes me that all these functions should return error conditions,
and the script be written to handle such errors gracefully.  Did the
author assume that a mail transfer will always execute without error?

--

At 05:55 PM 7/15/2002 -0330, jon writeth:
>Do you happen to have any Perl syntax for sending and e-mail through a
script for your 
>program smtpsend?

Use the system() command.  Be sure to grab the output (if any) and display
it to the user.  If there is no output, the e-mail was sent successfully.
Nuclear Vision allows for refined control of the e-mail building and
sending process with detailed error messages when they occur.

Type smtpsend -? at the command-line for detailed help.  Also, the
readme.txt file describes program usage.  SMTPSEND is a sub-set freeware
program of Nuclear Vision and only demonstrates a very small portion of the
power of Nuclear Vision.

-----Original Message-----
From: xitami-admin@lists.xitami.org
[mailto:xitami-admin@lists.xitami.org] On Behalf Of Ervin Kosch
Sent: Thursday, July 11, 2002 11:07 AM
To: xitami@lists.xitami.org
Subject: Re: [Xitami] IP numbers,etc.


You've graduated from webhost 101 to 201 now.

You have several options:
    1. Buy a static IP from your ISP.  If your ISP supports static(not 
changing) IP's that you'll pay anywhere from $ .01 to $20 extra a month.
    2. Get a DNS forwarding service.  These service work by linking a 
third level domain(Example: myname.tzo.com) to your IP address.  You 
then put a little program on your server. That program will every few 
minutes yells out to the service and say "I'm here" so to keep you IP# 
fresh. If watch this mail list people will give you serveral services. 
 I personally like TZO.com but other like DNS2GO.com and ww.myserver.org

work just as well..  Depending on the level of service the offer the 
services will run you from free to $100/month.
    3. Make your own service.  I have a couple of domains that point to 
my home system.  So if someone types in home.yumyum.ws they hit my main 
server which then redirectes them to my server in my house.

That is somebody who has a good old copy of  the Nimda virus running. 
 Nimda works by flooding your server's buffers.  Once the buffer is over 
flowed someone could insert functional computer code onto your system.

Xitami isn't directly effected by the virus, rather it either ignore the 
request and goes on or crashes.  I know that my 2.4d9 is perty good at 
handling Nimda.  2.5 anything is not the best.

What version are you running?

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Jul 16 16:43:44 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul Reid)
Date: Tue, 16 Jul 2002 11:43:44 -0400
Subject: [Xitami] Why is this crashing me?
In-Reply-To: <3.0.5.32.20020715204139.00da9a98@vvm.com>
References: <3.0.5.32.20020715204139.00da9a98@vvm.com>
Message-ID: <41688948775.20020716114344@rci.rutgers.edu>

>  "GET /default.ida?NNNNNNNNNNNNN

I get thousands of these a week from all over the world. I'm not
crashing and other Xitami users here are handling it fine. It bloats
the log-files, that's all.

The over-sized request is a deliberate attempt to break into MS IIS
webserver. It is very specific to unpatched IIS and products based
on IIS; no other software can be be infected.

The over-sized request can confuse and crash some non-IIS software
that never expected over-sized requests. Several network printers
and some routers lock-up or die after one of these.

Unlike IIS, written by children, and printers with a web interface
that is only a frill, Xitami was written by adults who won't take
candy from strangers without examining it carefully and safely.
Request buffers are checked and don't overflow. And even if they
did, the code that Red/Nimda tries to inject would not run in Xitami
because it needs to hit a specific place in IIS's code.

>  this always seems to be the last entry in the log

At the height of these epidemics, over half of my logs were
Red/Nimda requests. On a low-traffic server, the odds are high that
the "last log entry" would be one of these.

Xitami sometimes has trouble rotating its logs, a problem that gets
worse when under heavy traffic as from these epidemics. Especially
on Windows which does get sluggish with thousands of files in one
folder. It seems to help to clear out any temporary or odd-name
files in the logs and temp folders.

Do you have a second machine that is networked, always on, and has
Perl? I have a little script to read a web page at intervals and
report if it isn't there (or does not have an expected phrase, to
distinguish the right response from error-messages). That would
narrow down the actual time of crash.

 -PRR

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Jul 16 21:16:53 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Michael Bronder)
Date: Tue, 16 Jul 2002 16:16:53 -0400
Subject: [Xitami] Site listing for search engines
In-Reply-To: <F54PauDUUKbbudEijv900013086@hotmail.com>
Message-ID: <000601c22d05$ba6fca10$6400a8c0@Server>

it is an arcane science, akin to alchemy, getting listed in the engines.
There are folks who will charge you money to do it but here there are 2 esy
ways, aside from the meta-tag and wait method.

1) make firends with the appropriate category editor at dmoz.org, the Open
Directory Project.  Once a site is in there (well, after a couple weeks) it
get's populated to all the sites that license the directory.  Categories are
edited by volunteers.  If there isn't someone for your category, volunteer
yourself.

2) sign up for Lycos's InSite service which get's you into their version of
the FAST catalog, and will also give you a search utility to run on your
site.  There are other services, but an independant survey found lycos to be
the best for the money.

3) go to searchenginewatch.com and read up on it... many many strategies
there.

good luck

mb

you have it the syntax backwords. here's a cut from my default.cfg...

[Virtual-hosts]
    extranet.rcolmstead.com=extranet.cfg
    intranet.rcolmstead.com=intranet.cfg


which obviouly each points each vhost to their own config file..... this cut
is from the intranet config....

[Accesslog]
    Filename=intranet.log

[Security]
    Admin=0
    Filename=intranet.aut
    webmask=192.168.40.*

[Server]
    Webpages=d:\xitami\webpages

Use the ODBC SQL Server driver with whatever application you want to use.
You have to manually add databases to ODBC for each driver source you wish
to use, but once set up properly, you can use one code base for all databases.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Thu Jul 18 18:03:21 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Fabien Royer)
Date: Thu, 18 Jul 2002 13:03:21 -0400
Subject: [Xitami] FTP and FW-1
Message-ID: <F14492YLmogDOk2777s0000f403@hotmail.com>

Greg,

Your data channel is never being established because FW-1 is not letting the 
FTP server through to connect back to your client.

You can usually get around this problem by using your FTP client in passive 
mode, where the client initiates both command and data channels with the FTP 
server. However, this is going to require Firewall-1 to be configured to let 
a range of ports open to the FTP server.

While this is not a problem with a NAT-ted setup, you may encounter 
"political" management resistance ;-)

I hope this helps.

Regards,
Fabien.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Thu Jul 18 18:55:57 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (ian)
Date: Thu, 18 Jul 2002 13:55:57 -0400
Subject: [Xitami] FTP and FW-1
In-Reply-To: <F14492YLmogDOk2777s0000f403@hotmail.com>
Message-ID: <200207181757.g6IHvj4W014051@sxpublic.nxrda.imatix.net>

If you want to diagnose connection problems with your FTP server, you 
should be looking at your FW logs not the output of your FTP server. 
The logs will tell you more about what is going on and will show 
accepted and dropped packets.

FWIW: FW1 can handle passive connections just fine. Checkpoint has 
inspect code built in for the ftp service and can open the correct 
dynamic ports for each session.

There is a bug/limitation in earlier versions (even 4.1) of Checkpoint 
where the passive sessions for multiple files can eventually start 
running into the listed ports - then FW1 thinks that the dynamic port 
requests are invalid and will close the session. This only seems to 
happen with certain combinations of clients/servers and where they 
decide to start opening dynamic ports... just thought I would mention 
it, I don't use Xitami's ftp server, I got bit a long time ago by it 
and I have never forgiven it! I use ServU and have never had an issue 
and all my traffic goes through a Checkpoint FW.

More help for Checkpoint can be found either at their knowledge base or 
you can find a lot of great information at www.phoneboy.com

-Ian

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Jul 22 09:23:58 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Francis Turner)
Date: Mon, 22 Jul 2002 10:23:58 +0200
Subject: [Xitami] Defaults.aut
References: <3D39A147.277C0B9C@rogers.com>
Message-ID: <3D3BC11E.9060804@freesbee.fr>

Angelo Eatrides wrote:

>Hi all. 
>
>I need help with the xitamipro (evaluation version). 
>I need to assign a password protected directory on
>a virtual domain but I don't know how to define
>the directory in the defaults.aut. 
>
>I know [Private] will point to the private directory of
>the "webpages" dir but the dir I want to protect is above it
>off the main xitami root. 
>
>For example:  Xitami/example/private/
>  
>

You need to define an alias first and then password protetc the alias

i.e. in defualts.cgf have a line under alias called

Private = "C:/xitami/example/private"

And then in defaults.aut have (webmask is optional)

[Prvate]
    Userid = "password"
    Webmask = "ip.add.re.ss"

Francis

>
>123.456.789.123 - user [22/Jul/2002:13:28:07 +0000] "GET
>/video_k/newtest.wmv-getrightdownload HTTP/1.1" 404 0

Xitami is just attempting to open a file called (assuming default install):

c:\xitami\webpages\video_k\newtest.wmv-getrightdownload

If this file does not exist, you will get a 404 error.

>Any other ideas?
>> >to use a download manager. Is resume supported?

Considering that the headers Xitami returns does not have the
'Accept-Ranges' header in them, I would have to say that the answer is
'no'.  However, my answer is non-authoritative in this aspect...Ewen?

Hope this helps!

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Jul 24 17:14:39 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Thomas J. Hruska)
Date: Wed, 24 Jul 2002 12:14:39 -0400
Subject: [Xitami] Getright
In-Reply-To: <OE144D3MBhe3WYIgoFT00000c48@hotmail.com>
References: <3D39A147.277C0B9C@rogers.com>
 <OE32s5FGJziWwSoRKbp000076cb@hotmail.com>
 <004401c23295$124c2050$0200a8c0@p667>
Message-ID: <3.0.6.32.20020724121439.00a51ed0@mail.shininglightpro.com>

At 03:20 PM 7/24/2002 +0100, Kev writeth:
>Thanks - now all I need to do it get ftp working ;-(
>
>I am able to connect when I am within my home nework, but not from outside..
>
>I have set up my DSL router to forward port 21 to port 21 on the machine
>with the ftp server.
>
>I am using passive mode on my the far end.

Disable passive mode on your FTP client.  Unless it is "smart" enough to
understand protocol level commands, it won't allow anything through.  Your
end node has to accept connections through its firewall/routers or you
won't be able to do FTP data transfers.

>The far end seems to connect then tries to read the contents of the folder -
>it then times out and gives an error.

Disabling passive mode should fix this problem.  If it doesn't, then you
won't be able to FTP either way since there are two firewalls not willing
to talk to each other in the way.  You can try setting up a range of FTP
ports for incoming traffic to the server, but that opens a whole other
security issue that I don't have time to deal with.

Hope this helps!


          Thomas J. Hruska -- shinelight@shininglightpro.com
Shining Light Productions -- "Meeting the needs of fellow programmers"
                  http://www.shininglightpro.com/

Hi guys,

A newbie question:

I am using xitami as web server working with an app
server.  The function of the webserver are: receive
all port 80 calls, virtual hosting.

We have set up an index.htm page for each virtual
websites.  From the index page, a java script
re-direct to another page run by the app server.  The
app server take port address 8080 calls.

ie
sample.com points to ip, 66.66.66.01
Xitami pick up the call and point to: index.htm
http://sample.com shows index.htm and jump to 
66.66.66.01:8080/servlet/sample/home.jsp

how can i make it transparent so that home.jsp will
show as http://sample.com/servlet/home.jsp instead of
showing ip address and port?

Thanks
Just

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Jul 26 01:32:21 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (garry)
Date: Fri, 26 Jul 2002 12:32:21 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] Newbie question
References: <20020726002114.24655.qmail@web11303.mail.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <006701c2343b$e8141420$123d60cb@cable.net.nz>

You could use a frame on the first page and open the second in the frame.

The address of the frame will be shown then and none of your subsequent
address changes will show.

#   -------------------------------------------------------------------------
#   SSI configuration section
#
#   This section controls Xitami's built-in server-side includes (SSI)
#   handling.

[Ssi]
#   Lets you enable/disable SSI handling.

    enabled=1

#   Specifies the format for times shown by SSI pages.

    timefmt=%A, %d-%b-%y %H:%M:%S %Z

#   Specifies whether size should be shown as bytes or as
#   abbreviations (Kb, Mg). Anything other than the string "bytes" is
#   taken to mean that sizes are shown as abbreviations.

    sizefmt=bytes

#   The timeout for CGI programs called from the SSI agent.

    timeout=30

#   Error message shown when an SSI command fails. The %s symbol is
#   replaced by the cause of the problem.

    errmsg=<p>[xitami SSI: %s]

#   If 1, allows CGIs to be executed using the #exec command. Since
#   this is a security weakness, this option is switched-off by
#   default.

    exec=1

[end snippet]

Thanks,
