From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Jul 26 10:57:03 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Francis Turner)
Date: Fri, 26 Jul 2002 11:57:03 +0200
Subject: [Xitami] Newbie question
References: <20020726084433.2391.qmail@web11307.mail.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <3D411CEF.2000901@freesbee.fr>

This is a multi-part message in MIME format.
--------------030007090306010706080102
Content-Type: text/plain; charset=us-ascii; format=flowed
Content-Transfer-Encoding: 7bit

just fun wrote:

>Thanks Garry,
>
>Is that the only way? company doesn't encourage frame
>
>  
>
The only other way is to run the servlets direct from Xitami using the 
servlet runner at http://runner.conacom.de

If you do a web redirect then the browser will show the URI of the new 
location unless you use a frame.

If you want to do frames/redirects then you can do it server side 
insetad of client side using GSL / XML if you have xitami 2.5b5.

The enclosed script will do this and shoud be self explanatory

Francis

-- 
...if the US Government were ever to get really serious about Internet 
security, the top players in Microsoft's management hierarchy would find 
themselves handcuffed, blindfolded, led onto a tarmac within some obscure 
Air Force base, and shot.
-- Thomas C Greene (http://www.theregister.co.uk/content/55/23223.html)



--------------030007090306010706080102
Content-Type: text/plain;
 name="relo.gsl"
Content-Transfer-Encoding: 7bit
Content-Disposition: inline;
 filename="relo.gsl"

.-----------------------------------------------------------------------------
.-
.-  Relocator
.-
.-  Written:  2001/12/12  Francis Turner
.-  Modified: 2002/07/26  Francis Turner
.-
.-  Redirects you to another port on the same server. Either as a redirect or
.-  as an embedded frame. You can call it in 2 ways: either call direct 
.-    relo.gsl?p=PPP&m=C&t=TTT
.-    where PPP is the port for the redirect
.-    C is either an R for redirect or an F for frame
.-    TTT is a title used to give the frame mode a title. It is ignored in R mode
.-  or use as the script for a service.xml script
.-    e.g. a SWAT service redirector would look like
.-    <RELO SCRIPT='/relo.gsl'>
.-      <SERVICE NAME='Swat' PORT='901' MODE='FRAME'/>
.-    </RELO>
.-
.-  Modification allows you to do redrects to remote servers too using 
.-  either relo.gsl?u=URI&m=C&t=TTT or 
.-    <RELO SCRIPT='/relo.gsl'>
.-      <SERVICE NAME='Remote Server' MODE='FRAME'
.-        URI='http://remote.example.com/path/to/somewhere.html' />
.-    </RELO>
.-  Note that the direct call method will not cope well with URIs that have 
.-  their own query strings (i.e. URIs of the form http://some/where?query )
.-
.-----------------------------------------------------------------------------
<HTML><HEAD>
.- 
.- First deal with the case when called from XXX.xml
.- 
.if filename <> script
.  for service
.    mode ?= 'r'
.    port ?= 80
.    name ?= "Relo "+ port 
.    if (substr(mode,0,1,) = "f") | (substr(mode,0,,1) = "F")
<TITLE>$(name:)</TITLE></HEAD>
<FRAMESET cols="*">
.      if defined(uri)
  <FRAME name="In" src="$(uri:)">
.      else
  <FRAME name="In" src="http://$(HTTP_HOST:lower):$(port:)/">
.      endif
  <NOFRAMES>
  <H1>Sorry!</H1>
  <H3>This page must be viewed by a browser that is capable of viewing frames.</H3>
  </NOFRAMES>
</FRAMESET></HTML>
.    else
.      if defined(uri)
  <meta http-equiv="Refresh" content="0; URL=$(uri:)"></HEAD>
.      else
  <meta http-equiv="Refresh" content="0; URL=http://$(HTTP_HOST:lower):$(port:)/"></HEAD>
.      endif
  <BODY></BODY></HTML>
.-  <BODY>$(port?:)=$(name?:)=$(mode?:)-$(substr(mode,0,,1):)
.- </BODY></HTML>
.    endif
.  endfor
.- 
.- Now deal with the case when called direct as relo.gsl?p=PPP&m=C&t=TTT
.- 
.elsif defined(p)
.  m ?= 'r'
.  if substr(m,0,1,) = 'r'
<meta http-equiv="Refresh" content="0; URL=http://$(HTTP_HOST:lower):$(p:)/"></HEAD>
<BODY></BODY></HTML>
.  else
.    t ?= "Relo "+p
<TITLE>$(t:)</TITLE></HEAD>
<FRAMESET cols="*">
  <FRAME name="In" src="http://$(HTTP_HOST:lower):$(p:)/">
  <NOFRAMES>
  <H1>Sorry!</H1>
  <H3>This page must be viewed by a browser that is capable of viewing frames.</H3>
  </NOFRAMES>
</FRAMESET></HTML>
.  endif
.- 
.- Now deal with the case when called direct as relo.gsl?u=URI&m=C&t=TTT
.- 
.elsif defined(u)
.  m ?= 'r'
.  if substr(m,0,1,) = 'r'
<meta http-equiv="Refresh" content="0; URL=$(u:)"></HEAD>
<BODY></BODY></HTML>
.  else
.    t ?= "Relo "+u
<TITLE>$(t:)</TITLE></HEAD>
<FRAMESET cols="*">
  <FRAME name="In" src="$(u:)">
  <NOFRAMES>
  <H1>Sorry!</H1>
  <H3>This page must be viewed by a browser that is capable of viewing frames.</H3>
  </NOFRAMES>
</FRAMESET></HTML>
.  endif
.else
</HEAD><BODY>Bad Boy</BODY></HTML>
.endif

--------------030007090306010706080102--

Or you can use ZoneEdit's cloaking function. What it does is once the person
hits the redirected page, the address stays in the address bar, granted you
use the virtual domain for all your linking.

the first five domains.

Just another option.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Jul 29 23:44:38 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul Reid)
Date: Mon, 29 Jul 2002 18:44:38 -0400
Subject: [Xitami] Xitami under Mandrake
In-Reply-To: <006201c2374f$7e792d90$2c182341@crestron>
References: <006201c2374f$7e792d90$2c182341@crestron>
Message-ID: <60864081693.20020729184438@rci.rutgers.edu>

> When I ping localhost, I get the following (I assume this means
> its responding):

ping is a completely different service from HTTP. Many machines ping
without any web server. You have only proved that the network stack
is not totally boogered.

>  It comes up as an executable icon in KDE.

Oh your Windows boys. Not that I am any sort of unix-head.... more
like an MS-DOS head.

Don't believe everything, sometimes not anything, a GUI shows you.
Just because a file is tagged executable does not mean that just
running it is going to do any good. Try running `more'. Utterly
useless until you give it something to do.

> how do I "run" Xitami

Open a unix command window (some call it a shell prompt). No, do not
ask me where a GUI unix hides the command line. Sometimes you have
to telnet to itself. Then issue these commands. Remember that unix
is case-fussy!

 cd /usr/xitami-24d9
 Xitami -h

See what it says. You probably have to start it with command line
switches to tell it what to do (which is why clicking pictures isn't
going to do any good).

 -PRR

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Jul 30 00:44:43 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Thomas J. Hruska)
Date: Mon, 29 Jul 2002 19:44:43 -0400
Subject: [Xitami] Xitami under Mandrake
In-Reply-To: <006801c23756$ff9c8c80$2c182341@crestron>

At 07:23 PM 7/29/2002 -0400, Control-Freak writeth:
>I understand that pinging has nothing to do with http.  I was just letting
>everyone know that the networking is properly configured.  I am not a
>beginner, I've been using computers for over 25 years.  I am just a beginner
>at Linux.  I imagined it was a shell command.  I just don't know the syntax.
>
>I tried running xitami from the prompt already using xitami and now I have
>tried xitami -h.  I am in the usr/xitami-24d9 directory.  I get the
>following:
>
>bash: xitami: command not found

Sounds like xitami is either not marked as executable or your path
information is set up incorrectly.  I'm going to assume the latter as it is
more likely (you can edit your .bashrc file later to add the proper
information to the path and change other default bash settings).

Try ./xitami from the usr/xitami-24d9 directory.

If xitami is not marked as executable (if it isn't, there is probably
something wrong with the build), try chmod 700'ing the file.

Hope this helps!


          Thomas J. Hruska -- shinelight@shininglightpro.com
Shining Light Productions -- "Meeting the needs of fellow programmers"
                  http://www.shininglightpro.com/

> >I tried running xitami from the prompt already using xitami and now I
have
> >tried xitami -h.  I am in the usr/xitami-24d9 directory.  I get the
> >following:
> >
> >bash: xitami: command not found

> Sounds like xitami is either not marked as executable or your path
> information is set up incorrectly.  I'm going to assume the latter as it
is
> more likely (you can edit your .bashrc file later to add the proper
> information to the path and change other default bash settings).
>
> Try ./xitami from the usr/xitami-24d9 directory.
>

> something wrong with the build), try chmod 700'ing the file.

> Hope this helps!

/etc/rc.local.

When you boot it will start up Xitami as root, that is what I do 
on my machine.

Hi,

> (running on Win2K with SP2) that shuts down Xitami and >tells me that an

Just to exclude this as a possible cause. I once read the security help for
Win2k and follow the advise that one should use his workstation with power
user rights rather than administrator and log on as administrator only when
needed. I tried and couldn't keep it even for a day. Among other things,
xitami would behave totally out of whack when I tried to play with it logged
on as a power user account.

You don't run by any chance xitami service with other than system rights or
log on as a power user, are you?

Hope this helps

Stefan

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Jul 31 07:23:26 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Thomas J. Hruska)
Date: Wed, 31 Jul 2002 02:23:26 -0400
Subject: [Xitami] ProtoNova v1.0 Released! (And a XiFusion note)
In-Reply-To: <1027645077@coconutcomm.com>
References: <1027521048@coconutcomm.com>
Message-ID: <3.0.6.32.20020731022326.009f6930@mail.shininglightpro.com>

Due to the fact that many people here using the Xitami webserver are
looking for alternatives to Xitami since it no longer is a supported web
server (by the parent company iMatix), Shining Light Productions has
written a brand new web server called ProtoNova.

ProtoNova features:

  SSL/TLS support (with a simple-to-use SSL certificate generation system!)
  Normal HTTP/1.1 support
  Remote module support (moves heavy-duty processing off of the main server)
  A CGI remote module
  A LRWP remote module (allows you to directly move all current LRWP
applications to ProtoNova without recompiling!)
  A ColdFusion remote module (uses technology from XiFusion!)
  Database driven logs via ODBC (no log files!)
  Symbolic links
  Aliases
  Virtual hosting
  Multiple server support (multiple servers on multiple ports using one
application instance)
  Works "out-of-the-box"
  Secure "out-of-the-box"
  Extremely small footprint (runs on 16-32MB machines just fine...remote
modules can be used to dump the real workload onto better machines).
  ... And much, much more!


ProtoNova is a natural move from Xitami that offers server farm,
load-balancing, and clustering capabilities for a fraction of the price of
Xitami/Pro.  Also, while maintaining ease-of-use, the power of many
commercial servers can be found in simple, sensible configuration files.
Servers and virtual hosts can be brought on and offline without ever
stopping the server (the server detects the configuration change and loads
it up), which results in uptimes that can potentially exceed most (all?)
other web servers.

(Right now ProtoNova is only for Windows in a console, but eventually other
ports will become available.  The first port will be a Linux
port...probably RedHat).

For more information, visit the Shining Light Productions website:
<http://www.shininglightpro.com/index.php?treeloc=24>

Check out the ProtoNova Web Server today!


Note to XiFusion users:  XiFusion is still supported by Shining Light
Productions as it is a fairly popular freeware product.  However, the limit
to which XiFusion can be updated is quickly coming to a close (both OS and
calling process limitations are constantly arising).  Xitami is poorly
designed in the CGI arena and needs serious re-working to get rid of the
DoS/DDoS attack that still affects it.  ProtoNova is a viable alternative
that avoids the CGI DoS that plagues Xitami.  CGIs also seem to run faster
under ProtoNova...probably due to the method of handling the data pump and
having true HTTP/1.1 support.

ProtoNova is just one more way that Shining Light Productions is "Meeting
the Needs of Fellow Programmers!"


          Thomas J. Hruska -- shinelight@shininglightpro.com
Shining Light Productions -- "Meeting the needs of fellow programmers"
                  http://www.shininglightpro.com/

I don't intend to do so, certainly not on the strength of a single
message.  Thomas has been very helpful to Xitami users on this list, and
with the expection of this one message all has other messages have been
about programs that work with Xitami, helping fill in the gaps between
what Xitami does and what users want to do (eg, use it with ColdFusion).

Obviously if there were continuing advertisements for a competing
webserver then it would be a cause for concern.  However a single
announcement of a new program that might be of use to users of an existing
program that isn't being updated is well within accepted netiquette
(based on a dozen or so years on the 'net).  

Thomas is right that Xitami really hasn't been maintained much (due to
lack of time) over the past few years -- IIRC the last minor update was
over a year ago, and the last major update was more than 2 years ago.
>From time to time there are plans to change this, but a lack of free
time often gets in the way of such good plans.

"Thomas J. Hruska" <shinelight@shininglightpro.com> wrote:

> Due to the fact that many people here using the Xitami webserver are
> looking for alternatives to Xitami since it no longer is a supported
> web server (by the parent company iMatix), Shining Light Productions
> has written a brand new web server called ProtoNova...

Thomas is most welcome to announce ProtoNova on this list, although 
any extended discussion should probably move to a dedicated list. :)

Personally I welcome this announcement.  It offers Xitami users a 
choice, which is always good, and it offers Xitami some competition, 
which is good in a world where most web servers are too large and too 
complex for normal people.

I'm curious as to whether Thomas used any Xitami code in the server, 
or whether 'brand new' means written from scratch.  Thomas, you might 
want to explain your decision to start something new rather than add 
or improve the existing body of code.  Just for interest.  Also, is 
your server open source, or closed?

Then, what do you mean by 'a fraction of the price'?  Xitami/Pro is 
not expensive at $99.  Far too cheap, really, since it does not even 
start to pay its way.  What does ProtoNova cost?

Lastly, and this is for the record, Xitami *is* supported, if slowly, 
and will continue to be part of the iMatix toolset for as long as 
iMatix exists, which I intend to be a long time.  Providing open 
source products just happens to be very time consuming, and time is 
something that growing businesses are always short of.

Thomas, I think we can continue this discussion on the Xitami list 
for a little while.

-
Pieter Hintjens
iMatix Corporation

----- Original Message -----
From: "Marcio Marchini" <mqm@magma.ca>
To: <xitami@lists.xitami.org>
Sent: Thursday, July 11, 2002 10:50 AM
Subject: RE: [Xitami] IP numbers,etc.


> | But I am wondering, is it possible to give a page
> | a more durable address - say, a URL or a domain
> | name? I'm sure the answer is yes, but can anyone
> | give me a pointer on how to make this happen?
>
>
> You can register a domain ($20 / year) and then use www.zoneedit.com to
host
> the DNS service for you (free).
>
> Then you configure the computer which has a dynamic IP to tell zoneedit
when
> its IP changes. I do that from a Linux box. I run a script every 10
minutes
> (because I do not have a hook for when my IP changes at the Linksys
router, so I
> just do it blindly / periodically). All it does is to visit a URL. Just by
> visiting that URL at ZoneEdit they update the IP address for my domain.
So, the
> name will be constant but the IP may change as often as you want. All this
is
> documented at ZoneEdit, you've got to read the instructions there.
>
> So, I just give friends the name for my computer (say www.mycomputer.com)
and
> they can connect to it, even though I have a dynamic IP with an ADSL
provider.
>
>
> marcio
>
>
> --
> Xitami Users Mailing List -- For Xitami support
> To unsubscribe: http://lists.xitami.org/mailman/listinfo/xitami
>

From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Vance Forste)

Subject: [Xitami] OT: PHP-Nuke?
References: <5.1.0.14.2.20020712011137.00aad380@pop.chello.at> <001001c228e8$300d0ac0$2c838282@vance2> <3.0.5.32.20020710192540.00da5de0@vvm.com> <5.1.0.14.2.20020711115443.00aabb18@pop.chello.at> <5.1.0.14.2.20020712104752.00aad008@pop.chello.at>

Let me start off by saying I agree with your opinions, portability is a must
with my apps and I probably could have gone in and changed the script as
well, but... for alot of users editing a package like Nuke this is NOT an
option (as a matter of fact some users should not even have keyboards) and
they would not have a clue on how to follow the source to fix it (or even
follow instructions). I'm not a PHP person I prefer perl for CGI so yes I
could have fumbled through it (and I did a bit) and got sick of  looking
for, at the time, the unknown.
XiFusion is a viable quick and dirty soulution for me. However if this was
Nukes authors solution to the problem then it's a poor solution.
Personally I think they could have done a few things better with Nuke, for
instance do you think requiring setting php_display_errors=Off is any
better. To me that's another mask... (Ok I know I'm going further OT here)
So XiFusion masks a problem without having to go fix someones elses mess and
I think it does a good job at it too...

should be just " cgi-bin " ;)

I am re-writing my web site and I want to make it more dynamic, using Perl
scripts to build page elements. I am using frames, each frame calls a .shtml
file which simply has an <!--#exec cgi="/cgi-bin/blahblah.pl"-->. So far, I
have 3 frames: a top header, a left menu area, and a main area.

When I run this on my laptop using Xitami, only 2 of the 3 frames get built,
never all 3, and it sometimes varies as to which 2 get displayed. The third
frame is visually blank, and it acts as if the .shtml file did not even get
parsed as clicking 'view source' on that frame gives me the source for the
frameset (index.html). I can eliminate any one frame and the other 2 will
always load correctly.

Now, I can load the whole she-bang on my web host server (Linux/Apache, I
think) and it all works just fine. URL is http://www.thunting.com/geotech2.
Does Xitami have problems with multiple SSI calls in frames?

Also, I'm only familiar with good ol' HTML and Perl, and JavaScript to a
lesser extent. Is there a better way to dynamically build relatively simple
web pages? For some of my stuff, I will parse data files to build page
content, other times I will just write the HTML code in a Perl script, which
allows me to use config files to alter the look & feel of the entire site. I
see discussions about PHP, which I know nothing about, but I'm reluctant to
invest a lot of time learning something entirely new for such a minor
project.

Also, in making web pages fully dynamic, it would seem that web search
spiders would not be able to "look" at the content of the pages. Is this
right? Is there a simple way to deal with this?

Many thanks,
Carl
